[gpui](index.html)

Struct Timer Copy item path
===========================

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#144)

```
pub struct Timer { /* private fields */ }
```

Expand description

A future or stream that emits timed events.

Timers are futures that output a single [`Instant`](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/time/struct.Instant.html "struct std::time::Instant") when they fire.

Timers are also streams that can output [`Instant`](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/time/struct.Instant.html "struct std::time::Instant")s periodically.

[§](#precision)Precision
------------------------

There is a limit on the maximum precision that a `Timer` can provide. This limit is
dependent on the current platform; for instance, on Windows, the maximum precision is
about 16 milliseconds. Because of this limit, the timer may sleep for longer than the
requested duration. It will never sleep for less.

[§](#examples)Examples
----------------------

Sleep for 1 second:

```
use async_io::Timer;
use std::time::Duration;

Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1)).await;
```

Timeout after 1 second:

```
use async_io::Timer;
use futures_lite::FutureExt;
use std::time::Duration;

let addrs = async_net::resolve("google.com:80")
    .or(async {
        Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1)).await;
        Err(std::io::ErrorKind::TimedOut.into())
    })
    .await?;
```

Implementations[§](#implementations)
------------------------------------

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#161)[§](#impl-Timer)

### impl [Timer](struct.Timer.html "struct gpui::Timer")

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#194)

#### pub fn [never](#method.never)() -> [Timer](struct.Timer.html "struct gpui::Timer") [ⓘ](#)

Creates a timer that will never fire.

##### [§](#examples-1)Examples

This function may also be useful for creating a function with an optional timeout.

```
use async_io::Timer;
use futures_lite::prelude::*;
use std::time::Duration;

async fn run_with_timeout(timeout: Option<Duration>) {
    let timer = timeout
        .map(|timeout| Timer::after(timeout))
        .unwrap_or_else(Timer::never);

    run_lengthy_operation().or(timer).await;
}

// Times out after 5 seconds.
run_with_timeout(Some(Duration::from_secs(5))).await;
// Does not time out.
run_with_timeout(None).await;
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#214)

#### pub fn [after](#method.after)(duration: [Duration](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/time/struct.Duration.html "struct core::time::Duration")) -> [Timer](struct.Timer.html "struct gpui::Timer") [ⓘ](#)

Creates a timer that emits an event once after the given duration of time.

##### [§](#examples-2)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use std::time::Duration;

Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1)).await;
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#234)

#### pub fn [at](#method.at)(instant: [Instant](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/time/struct.Instant.html "struct std::time::Instant")) -> [Timer](struct.Timer.html "struct gpui::Timer") [ⓘ](#)

Creates a timer that emits an event once at the given time instant.

##### [§](#examples-3)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use std::time::{Duration, Instant};

let now = Instant::now();
let when = now + Duration::from_secs(1);
Timer::at(when).await;
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#252)

#### pub fn [interval](#method.interval)(period: [Duration](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/time/struct.Duration.html "struct core::time::Duration")) -> [Timer](struct.Timer.html "struct gpui::Timer") [ⓘ](#)

Creates a timer that emits events periodically.

##### [§](#examples-4)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use futures_lite::StreamExt;
use std::time::{Duration, Instant};

let period = Duration::from_secs(1);
Timer::interval(period).next().await;
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#273)

#### pub fn [interval\_at](#method.interval_at)(start: [Instant](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/time/struct.Instant.html "struct std::time::Instant"), period: [Duration](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/time/struct.Duration.html "struct core::time::Duration")) -> [Timer](struct.Timer.html "struct gpui::Timer") [ⓘ](#)

Creates a timer that emits events periodically, starting at `start`.

##### [§](#examples-5)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use futures_lite::StreamExt;
use std::time::{Duration, Instant};

let start = Instant::now();
let period = Duration::from_secs(1);
Timer::interval_at(start, period).next().await;
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#319)

#### pub fn [will\_fire](#method.will_fire)(&self) -> [bool](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/primitive.bool.html)

Indicates whether or not this timer will ever fire.

[`never()`](struct.Timer.html#method.never "associated function gpui::Timer::never") will never fire, and timers created with [`after()`](struct.Timer.html#method.after "associated function gpui::Timer::after") or [`at()`](struct.Timer.html#method.at "associated function gpui::Timer::at") will fire
if the duration is not too large.

##### [§](#examples-6)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use futures_lite::prelude::*;
use std::time::Duration;

// `never` will never fire.
assert!(!Timer::never().will_fire());

// `after` will fire if the duration is not too large.
assert!(Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1)).will_fire());
assert!(!Timer::after(Duration::MAX).will_fire());

// However, once an `after` timer has fired, it will never fire again.
let mut t = Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1));
assert!(t.will_fire());
(&mut t).await;
assert!(!t.will_fire());

// Interval timers will fire periodically.
let mut t = Timer::interval(Duration::from_secs(1));
assert!(t.will_fire());
t.next().await;
assert!(t.will_fire());
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#340)

#### pub fn [set\_after](#method.set_after)(&mut self, duration: [Duration](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/time/struct.Duration.html "struct core::time::Duration"))

Sets the timer to emit an event once after the given duration of time.

Note that resetting a timer is different from creating a new timer because
[`set_after()`](struct.Timer.html#method.set_after "method gpui::Timer::set_after") does not remove the waker associated with the task
that is polling the timer.

##### [§](#examples-7)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use std::time::Duration;

let mut t = Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1));
t.set_after(Duration::from_millis(100));
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#370)

#### pub fn [set\_at](#method.set_at)(&mut self, instant: [Instant](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/time/struct.Instant.html "struct std::time::Instant"))

Sets the timer to emit an event once at the given time instant.

Note that resetting a timer is different from creating a new timer because
[`set_at()`](struct.Timer.html#method.set_at "method gpui::Timer::set_at") does not remove the waker associated with the task
that is polling the timer.

##### [§](#examples-8)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use std::time::{Duration, Instant};

let mut t = Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1));

let now = Instant::now();
let when = now + Duration::from_secs(1);
t.set_at(when);
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#402)

#### pub fn [set\_interval](#method.set_interval)(&mut self, period: [Duration](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/time/struct.Duration.html "struct core::time::Duration"))

Sets the timer to emit events periodically.

Note that resetting a timer is different from creating a new timer because
[`set_interval()`](struct.Timer.html#method.set_interval "method gpui::Timer::set_interval") does not remove the waker associated with the
task that is polling the timer.

##### [§](#examples-9)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use futures_lite::StreamExt;
use std::time::{Duration, Instant};

let mut t = Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1));

let period = Duration::from_secs(2);
t.set_interval(period);
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#433)

#### pub fn [set\_interval\_at](#method.set_interval_at)(&mut self, start: [Instant](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/time/struct.Instant.html "struct std::time::Instant"), period: [Duration](https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/time/struct.Duration.html "struct core::time::Duration"))

Sets the timer to emit events periodically, starting at `start`.

Note that resetting a timer is different from creating a new timer because
[`set_interval_at()`](struct.Timer.html#method.set_interval_at "method gpui::Timer::set_interval_at") does not remove the waker associated with
the task that is polling the timer.

##### [§](#examples-10)Examples

```
use async_io::Timer;
use futures_lite::StreamExt;
use std::time::{Duration, Instant};

let mut t = Timer::after(Duration::from_secs(1));

let start = Instant::now();
let period = Duration::from_secs(2);
t.set_interval_at(start, period);
```

[Source](https://docs.rs/async-io/2.6.0/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/src/async_io/lib.rs.html#446)

#### pub fn [clear](#method.clear)(&mut self)

Clear any timeouts set on this timer. It will never fire again until a new interval or instant is set.
